It provides a complete HTTP server implementation with integrated authentication, authorization, admission control, audit logging, storage abstraction, and lifecycle management. The architecture follows a layered, composable design where HTTP requests pass through a middleware chain before reaching REST handlers backed by configurable storage.\n\nThis document provides an in-depth analysis of the apiserver subsystem, including its architecture, component responsibilities, request-path flow, extension points, and operational considerations.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### Purpose\n\nThe apiserver library solves the core problem of implementing a Kubernetes-compatible HTTP API server. Rather than requiring each API server implementation to build authentication, authorization, admission, audit, storage, and lifecycle management from scratch, this library provides:\n\n- **Unified authentication/authorization**: Support for multiple auth strategies (tokens, certs, OIDC, etc.)\n- **Admission control chain**: Pre/post-write validation and mutation via plugins and webhooks\n- **Audit logging**: Comprehensive request/response logging for compliance and debugging\n- **HTTP routing and REST semantics**: RESTful operations on Kubernetes objects\n- **Graceful lifecycle management**: Startup hooks, pre-shutdown coordination, and draining\n- **Discovery and API documentation**: OpenAPI v2/v3 endpoints and API group discovery\n- **Storage abstraction**: Pluggable backends (etcd, custom implementations)\n- **Observability**: Health checks (readiness, liveness), metrics, profiling, status endpoints\n\n### Subsystem Boundaries\n\n**Internal (within apiserver library):**\n- Request middleware chain (filters, authentication, authorization, audit)\n- REST handler implementations (create, read, update, delete, watch, list)\n- Admission plugin coordination\n- Server lifecycle (startup hooks, graceful shutdown)\n- Discovery and OpenAPI generation\n\n**External (provided by consumers):**\n- Storage backend implementation (`k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/storage/Interface`)\n- Resource definitions (via `APIGroupInfo` with storage mappings)\n- Custom authentication/authorization strategies\n- Custom admission plugins\n- HTTP listener configuration (TLS certs, port binding)\n\n### Upstream Dependencies\n\nThe apiserver depends on:\n\n1. **`k8s.io/apimachinery`** - Core Kubernetes types, runtime, serialization\n2. **`k8s.io/component-base`** - Shared utilities (feature gates, cli flags, etc.)\n3. **`k8s.io/klog`** - Structured logging\n4. **`k8s.io/kube-openapi`** - OpenAPI v2/v3 generation and serving\n5. **`golang.org/x/time/rate`** - Rate limiting infrastructure\n6. **`go-restful`** - REST handler framework\n7. **Standard library** - HTTP, sync, context, etc.\n\n### Downstream Dependencies\n\nConsumers of apiserver include:\n\n1. **`k8s.io/kubernetes`** (kube-apiserver) - Primary consumer with all Kubernetes built-in resource types\n2. **`k8s.io/kube-aggregator`** - API aggregation server for delegating requests to extension servers\n3. **`k8s.io/apiextensions-apiserver`** - Custom Resource Definition (CRD) server\n4. **Extension API servers** - Any server implementing custom resources (service catalog, etc.)\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Server Infrastructure\n\n#### GenericAPIServer (`pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` lines 108-304)\n\nThe central orchestrator containing:\n\n```go\ntype GenericAPIServer struct {\n    Handler *APIServerHandler           // HTTP request handler chain\n    admissionControl admission.Interface // Admission plugin chain\n    Authorizer authorizer.Authorizer     // Authorization decision maker\n    AuditBackend audit.Backend           // Audit event logging\n    LoopbackClientConfig *rest.Config    // Privileged internal client\n    SecureServingInfo *SecureServingInfo // TLS configuration\n    // ... lifecycle hooks, health checks, storage, discovery managers\n}\n```\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Holds all server-level state\n- Provides lifecycle methods: `PrepareRun()`, `RunWithContext()`, `Shutdown()`\n- Registers API groups and resources\n- Manages HTTP listener and request routing\n- Orchestrates graceful shutdown with draining\n\n#### Config (`pkg/server/config.go` lines 110-300)\n\nImmutable configuration passed at server creation:\n\n```go\ntype Config struct {\n    SecureServing *SecureServingInfo\n    Authentication AuthenticationInfo\n    Authorization AuthorizationInfo\n    AdmissionControl admission.Interface\n    AuditBackend audit.Backend\n    RequestTimeout time.Duration\n    MinRequestTimeout time.Duration\n    HealthzChecks []healthz.HealthChecker\n    BuildHandlerChainFunc func(handler.Interface, *Config) http.Handler\n    // ... serializers, codecs, validators\n}\n```\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Provides defaults for all server configuration\n- Validated during `Complete()` transition\n- Builds the handler chain via customizable builder function\n- Defines request timeout policies\n\n### 2.2 Request Routing and Handler Chain\n\n#### APIServerHandler (`pkg/server/handler.go` lines 42-67)\n\nRoutes incoming HTTP requests:\n\n```go\ntype APIServerHandler struct {\n    FullHandlerChain http.Handler           // Complete middleware stack\n    GoRestfulContainer *restful.Container   // API endpoints\n    NonGoRestfulMux *pathrecorder.PathRecorderMux // Non-API routes\n    Director http.Handler                  // Request router\n}\n```\n\n**Request flow through APIServerHandler.ServeHTTP:**\n1. Passes request through `FullHandlerChain` (all filters)\n2. `Director` examines path to determine handler:\n   - If REST API path → routes to `GoRestfulContainer` (go-restful framework)\n   - Otherwise → routes to `NonGoRestfulMux` (static routes, fallback)\n\n#### Handler Chain Building (`pkg/server/config.go` lines 1015-1097)\n\n`DefaultBuildHandlerChain` constructs the middleware stack in execution order:\n\n1. **Panic Recovery** - Catches and logs panics before they crash server\n2. **Audit Init** - Initializes audit event object with request metadata\n3. **Mux Complete** - Waits for all routes to be registered before accepting requests\n4. **Request Timestamp** - Records when request arrived (for latency tracking)\n5. **Request Info** - Parses request into RequestInfo (resource, verb, namespace, name, etc.)\n6. **Routine** - (Optional) Executes handler in separate goroutine\n7. **Latency Trackers** - Tracks request latency metrics\n8. **HTTP Logging** - Logs HTTP requests at configured verbosity\n9. **Retry-After** - (Optional during shutdown) Sends 429 status\n10. **HSTS Headers** - Adds HTTP Strict-Transport-Security header\n11. **HTTP/2 Goaway** - (Optional) Sends periodic goaway frames to drain connections\n12. **Watch Termination** - (Optional during shutdown) Drains watch connections gracefully\n13. **Wait Group Tracking** - Tracks active requests for graceful shutdown\n14. **Request Deadline** - Applies per-request timeout from query param\n15. **Timeout for Non-Long-Running** - Applies default timeout for list/get/create requests\n16. **Warning Recorder** - Records deprecation and warning headers\n17. **CORS** - Cross-origin resource sharing policy\n18. **Authentication** - User/service account identification via tokens/certs/etc.\n19. **Tracing** - (Optional) Distributed tracing context propagation\n20. **Failed Auth Audit** - Logs failed authentication attempts\n21. **Audit** - Logs request/response body and metadata\n22. **Impersonation** - Allows privileged users to act as other users\n23. **Priority and Fairness / Max In-Flight** - Rate limiting and request prioritization\n24. **Authorization** - Access control decision (RBAC, ABAC, webhook, etc.)\n25. **REST Handler** - Serves the actual REST endpoint\n\n### 2.3 Admission Control\n\n#### Admission Chain (`pkg/admission/chain.go` lines 23-70)\n\nProcesses requests in two phases:\n\n```go\ntype chainAdmissionHandler struct {\n    handlers []Interface // Ordered list of admission plugins\n}\n\n// Mutating phase: plugins can modify objects\nfunc (c *chainAdmissionHandler) Admit(attributes Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n\n// Validating phase: plugins validate final object state\nfunc (c *chainAdmissionHandler) Validate(attributes Attributes, o ObjectInterfaces) error\n```\n\n**Key properties:**\n- **Fail-closed**: Any plugin returning error rejects the request\n- **Ordered**: Execution order matters (specified at registration)\n- **Read-only validation**: Validating phase cannot modify objects\n- **Attributes available**: Request info (user, namespace, resource, operation) passed to all plugins\n\n**Supported plugins:**\n- Webhook plugins (mutating and validating)\n- Built-in plugins: PodSecurityPolicy, ResourceQuota, ServiceAccount, Namespace, LimitRanger, etc.\n\n**Admission integration** (`pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go`, `update.go`, `delete.go`):\n- Called after deserialization but before storage write\n- Receives object interfaces for conversion/defaulting\n- Can reject or mutate request objects\n\n### 2.4 Authentication and Authorization\n\n#### Authentication (`pkg/authentication/authenticator/interfaces.go`)\n\nIdentifies the user making the request:\n\n```go\ntype Response struct {\n    User user.Info              // Authenticated user (name, uid, groups, extra)\n    Audiences Audiences          // OAuth audiences if applicable\n}\n\ntype Token interface {\n    AuthenticateToken(ctx, token) (*Response, ok bool, err)\n}\n\ntype Request interface {\n    AuthenticateRequest(req *http.Request) (*Response, ok bool, err)\n}\n```\n\n**Multiple strategies combined:**\n- Token authenticators: Bearer tokens, bootstrap tokens\n- Request authenticators: Client certificates, HTTP basic auth, OIDC\n- All strategies tried; first success wins\n\n#### Authorization (`pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go`)\n\nDetermines if authenticated user can perform action:\n\n```go\ntype Attributes interface {\n    GetUser() user.Info\n    GetVerb() string                    // \"create\", \"get\", \"list\", \"watch\", \"delete\", etc.\n    GetResource() string                // \"pods\", \"services\", \"deployments\"\n    GetNamespace() string               // \"\" for cluster-scoped resources\n    GetName() string                    // Resource name if specified\n    GetAPIGroup() string                // API group\n    GetPath() string                    // HTTP path for non-resource requests\n}\n\ntype Decision int\nconst (\n    Allow Decision = iota\n    Deny\n    NoOpinion                           // Allows other authorizers to decide\n)\n\ntype Authorizer interface {\n    Authorize(ctx context.Context, attributes Attributes) (Decision, reason string, err error)\n}\n```\n\n**Multiple strategies:**\n- Union authorizer chains multiple implementations\n- Implementations: RBAC, ABAC, webhook, node authorization\n- Any Allow decision succeeds; explicit Deny fails\n\n### 2.5 Storage Abstraction\n\n#### Storage Interface (`pkg/storage/interfaces.go`)\n\nThe bridge between REST handlers and persistent storage:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n    Versioner() Versioner\n}\n\ntype Versioner interface {\n    UpdateObject(obj runtime.Object, resourceVersion string) error\n    ObjectResourceVersion(obj runtime.Object) (resourceVersion string, err error)\n}\n\ntype Lister interface {\n    List(ctx, key string, opts ListOptions) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n\ntype Getter interface {\n    Get(ctx, key string, opts GetOptions) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n\ntype Watcher interface {\n    Watch(ctx, key string, opts WatchOptions) (watch.Interface, error)\n}\n\ntype Creator interface {\n    Create(ctx, key string, obj, out runtime.Object, ttl time.Duration) error\n}\n\ntype Updater interface {\n    Update(ctx, key string, obj runtime.Object, ...) (runtime.Object, error)\n}\n```\n\n**Backend implementations:**\n- **etcd3** (`pkg/storage/etcd3/`): Primary backend using etcd as persistent store\n- **Cacher** (`pkg/storage/cacher/`): In-memory cache layer above backends\n- **Custom**: Consumers can implement custom backends\n\n**Key concepts:**\n- **Resource versions**: Opaque version identifiers (typically etcd revision numbers)\n- **Key structure**: `/namespace/resource/name` (keys are namespaced)\n- **Watchers**: Long-lived connections streaming object changes\n- **List consistency**: Can specify `resourceVersionMatch` (exact, NotOlderThan)\n\n### 2.6 REST Handlers\n\n#### Resource Installation (`pkg/endpoints/installer.go` lines 1-1400+)\n\n`APIInstaller` registers REST endpoints for a resource:\n\n```go\ntype APIInstaller struct {\n    group string\n    version string\n    kind string\n    storage map[string]rest.Storage  // Storage per resource type\n}\n\n// Creates web service with all REST routes\nfunc (a *APIInstaller) Install(container *restful.Container) error\n```\n\n**Routes registered per resource:**\n- `POST /api/v1/namespace/pods` → create handler\n- `GET /api/v1/namespace/pods/name` → get handler\n- `PATCH /api/v1/namespace/pods/name` → patch handler\n- `PUT /api/v1/namespace/pods/name` → update handler\n- `DELETE /api/v1/namespace/pods/name` → delete handler\n- `GET /api/v1/namespace/pods` → list handler\n- `GET /api/v1/namespace/pods?watch=true` → watch handler\n\n#### Handler Types (`pkg/endpoints/handlers/`)\n\n**Create Handler** (`create.go`):\n- Deserializes request body\n- Calls admission (mutating + validating)\n- Calls storage.Create()\n- Returns created object with 201 status\n\n**Get Handler** (`get.go`):\n- Retrieves single object by name\n- Returns 200 with object, or 404 if not found\n\n**List Handler** (`list.go`):\n- Lists all objects in namespace/cluster\n- Supports pagination (limit, continue)\n- Supports filtering by label/field selectors\n- Returns 200 with list object\n\n**Watch Handler** (`watch.go`):\n- Opens long-lived HTTP connection\n- Streams object changes as ADDED/MODIFIED/DELETED events\n- Supports resourceVersion to resume from specific point\n\n**Patch Handler** (`patch.go`):\n- Strategic merge patch or JSON patch\n- Applies changes to existing object\n- Calls admission (mutating + validating) on modified object\n\n**Update Handler** (`update.go`):\n- Full object replacement\n- Requires resourceVersion (optimistic concurrency control)\n- Calls admission (mutating + validating)\n\n### 2.7 Lifecycle Management\n\n#### Hooks System (`pkg/server/hooks.go`)\n\nTwo types of callbacks for server lifecycle:\n\n```go\ntype PostStartHook func(context.Context) error\ntype PreShutdownHook func() error\n```\n\n**PostStartHook usage:**\n- Registered via `AddPostStartHook(name, fn)`\n- Called in registration order after listener is ready\n- Blocking: server waits for all hooks to complete before serving requests\n- Used for: controller startup, cache sync, etc.\n\n**PreShutdownHook usage:**\n- Registered via `AddPreShutdownHook(name, fn)`\n- Called before graceful shutdown sequence\n- Blocking: server waits for all hooks to complete\n- Used for: final cleanup, resource release\n\n#### Graceful Shutdown (`pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` lines 525-650+)\n\n`RunWithContext(ctx)` manages shutdown sequence:\n\n1. **Listener starts**: HTTP server begins accepting requests\n2. **Post-start hooks run**: Called in order (blocking)\n3. **Request serving**: Handles incoming requests\n4. **Context cancellation detected**: External signal (Ctrl+C, k8s termination)\n5. **NotAcceptingNewRequest**: Stop accepting new requests (return 429 or timeout)\n6. **Wait for in-flight requests**: All non-watch requests must complete (with timeout)\n7. **Pre-shutdown hooks run**: Called in reverse order\n8. **HTTP server stops listening**: No new connections accepted\n9. **Audit backend drains**: Final audit events written\n10. **Context timeout occurs**: Hard deadline if graceful shutdown takes too long\n\n**Key variables:**\n- `ShutdownDelayDuration`: Wait before rejecting new requests (load balancer drain time)\n- `ShutdownTimeout`: Max time for entire graceful shutdown (default varies)\n- `NonLongRunningRequestWaitGroup`: Tracks non-watch requests\n- `WatchRequestWaitGroup`: Tracks watch connections\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control/Request Flow\n\n### 3.1 Server Initialization Sequence\n\n```\n1. NewRecommendedConfig()\n   └─ Creates Config with sensible defaults\n   └─ Location: pkg/server/config.go:397\n\n2. config.Complete(informers)\n   └─ Validates and finalizes configuration\n   └─ Returns completedConfig wrapper\n\n3. completedConfig.New(name, delegationTarget)\n   └─ Instantiates GenericAPIServer\n   └─ Creates APIServerHandler with handler chain\n   └─ Initializes admission, auth, authz, audit\n   └─ Registers delegation chain hooks\n   └─ Location: pkg/server/config.go:767\n\n4. InstallAPIGroups(apiGroupInfo...)\n   └─ For each API group:\n      ├─ installAPIResources()\n      ├─ getAPIGroupVersion()\n      ├─ APIGroupVersion.InstallREST()\n      │  └─ Creates go-restful WebService\n      │  └─ APIInstaller.Install() registers handlers per resource\n      │  └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/groupversion.go\n      └─ Registers with discovery manager\n   └─ Location: pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:1200+\n\n5. PrepareRun()\n   └─ Installs system routes:\n      ├─ /openapi/v2 (OpenAPI v2 spec)\n      ├─ /openapi/v3 (OpenAPI v3 spec)\n      ├─ /healthz, /readyz, /livez (health checks)\n      ├─ /metrics (Prometheus metrics)\n      ├─ /debug/pprof/* (profiling endpoints)\n      ├─ / (root index)\n   └─ Location: pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:440\n\n6. RunWithContext(ctx)\n   └─ Creates and starts HTTP server\n   └─ Runs PostStartHooks\n   └─ Blocks on request handling\n   └─ Implements graceful shutdown on context cancellation\n   └─ Location: pkg/server/genericapiserver.go:525\n```\n\n### 3.2 Single REST Request Lifecycle\n\nConcrete example: Creating a Pod\n\n```\nClient: POST /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods\n        Content-Type: application/json\n        Authorization: Bearer <token>\n        {pod specification}\n\n1. HTTPServer receives request\n   └─ Calls GenericAPIServer.Handler.ServeHTTP()\n\n2. FullHandlerChain Filters (in order):\n\n   a) PanicRecovery\n      └─ Wraps handler with recover()\n      └─ Location: pkg/server/filters/panic.go\n\n   b) AuditInit\n      └─ Creates audit.Event object\n      └─ Stores in request context\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go (init phase)\n\n   c) MuxComplete\n      └─ Waits for all routes to be registered\n      └─ Location: pkg/server/filters/mux.go\n\n   d) RequestReceivedTimestamp\n      └─ req.ctx += RequestReceivedTimestamp\n      └─ Location: pkg/server/filters/request_info.go\n\n   e) RequestInfo\n      └─ Parses request into RequestInfo:\n         - Resource: \"pods\"\n         - Verb: \"create\"\n         - Namespace: \"default\"\n         - APIGroup: \"\"\n         - APIVersion: \"v1\"\n      └─ Validates RequestInfo\n      └─ Rejects requests with malformed paths\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/filters/request_info.go\n      └─ Code: requestinfo.NewResolver() implementation\n\n   f) HTTPLogging\n      └─ Logs basic HTTP info (method, path, user agent)\n      └─ Location: pkg/server/filters/http_logging.go\n\n   g) CORS\n      └─ Adds Access-Control-* headers\n      └─ Location: pkg/server/filters/cors.go\n\n   h) TimeoutForNonLongRunning\n      └─ Sets request timeout from minRequestTimeout config\n      └─ Applies to list/get/create/update/patch (not watch)\n      └─ Location: pkg/server/filters/timeout.go\n\n   i) WithDeadline\n      └─ Applies timeout from http://example.com?timeout=30s\n      └─ Enforced via context.WithDeadline()\n      └─ Location: pkg/server/filters/request_deadline.go\n\n   j) Authentication\n      └─ Tries all configured authenticators in order:\n         - Bearer token authenticators\n         - Client certificate\n         - OIDC\n         - HTTP basic auth\n      └─ First successful authenticator wins\n      └─ Sets req.ctx.User to authenticated user.Info\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/filters/authentication.go\n      └─ Called authenticatorfactory.New() from config\n\n   k) Impersonation\n      └─ Checks Impersonate-User, Impersonate-Group headers\n      └─ Authorizer called to verify impersonation allowed\n      └─ Replaces req.ctx.User with impersonated identity\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/filters/impersonation/\n\n   l) Audit (logging phase)\n      └─ Populates audit.Event with request details:\n         - User\n         - Verb, Resource, Namespace\n         - Request body (if configured)\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go\n\n   m) PriorityAndFairness (or MaxInFlight)\n      └─ Rate limiting based on request characteristics\n      └─ Queues request if at capacity\n      └─ May reject with 429 if queue full\n      └─ Location: pkg/server/filters/priority_and_fairness.go\n\n   n) Authorization\n      └─ Creates Attributes from RequestInfo:\n         - Verb: \"create\"\n         - Resource: \"pods\"\n         - Namespace: \"default\"\n         - User: (authenticated user from filter j)\n      └─ Calls Authorizer.Authorize(ctx, attributes)\n      └─ Union of registered authorizers (RBAC, ABAC, webhook, etc.)\n      └─ Rejects with 403 Forbidden if Deny decision\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/filters/authorization.go\n\n3. Director Routes Request\n   └─ Examines path \"/api/v1/namespaces/default/pods\"\n   └─ Matches REST pattern → routes to GoRestfulContainer\n   └─ Location: pkg/server/handler.go:121-150\n\n4. REST Handler (Create)\n   └─ Deserialize request body using configured serializer\n      └─ body JSON → Pod object\n      └─ Validates API version matches expected version\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go:58-120\n\n   └─ Call storage.Get(key, existing) if needed for optimistic concurrency\n\n   └─ Admission - Mutating Phase\n      └─ admissionControl.Admit(attributes, objectInterfaces)\n      └─ All mutating plugins run in order\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go:125-140\n      └─ Plugins may:\n         - Modify pod spec (add labels, patches, security contexts)\n         - Inject environment variables\n         - Add volume mounts\n      └─ Any error from admission plugin returns 400 Bad Request\n\n   └─ Admission - Validating Phase\n      └─ admissionControl.Validate(attributes, objectInterfaces)\n      └─ All validating plugins run in order\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go:140-160\n      └─ Plugins may only validate, not modify\n      └─ Any error returns 400 Bad Request or custom status\n\n   └─ Call storage.Create(key, obj, out)\n      └─ etcd backend writes object\n      └─ Sets resource version (etcd revision)\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/handlers/create.go:165-180\n      └─ May fail with:\n         - 409 Conflict (already exists)\n         - 500 Server Error (etcd down)\n\n   └─ Audit Logging - Response Phase\n      └─ audit event enriched with:\n         - Response status (201 Created)\n         - Response object (if configured to log)\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/filters/audit.go\n\n   └─ Return HTTP 201 Created\n      └─ Body: created Pod object (serialized to JSON)\n      └─ Header: Content-Type: application/json\n      └─ Header: Location: /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods/mypod\n\n5. Response Sent to Client\n   └─ All response filters (audit, warning, etc.) complete\n   └─ HTTP 201 with Pod object\n\nTimeline:\n  T+0ms:    Request received at HTTP listener\n  T+1ms:    RequestInfo parsed (auth/authz cannot proceed without this)\n  T+2ms:    Authentication completed\n  T+3ms:    Authorization completed\n  T+4ms:    Admission plugins execute\n  T+5ms:    etcd write executed (network latency may dominate)\n  T+100ms:  Response sent\n  T+105ms:  Request complete, removed from wait group\n```\n\n**Critical request flow dependencies:**\n- RequestInfo MUST be parsed before authentication/authorization (they depend on resource/verb extraction)\n- Authentication MUST complete before authorization (authz depends on authenticated user)\n- Authorization MUST complete before admission (admission may need to know if request allowed)\n- Admission MUST complete before storage write (admission can reject request)\n\n### 3.3 Watch Request Lifecycle\n\nConcrete example: Watching Pod changes\n\n```\nClient: GET /api/v1/namespaces/default/pods?watch=true\n        Authorization: Bearer <token>\n\n1-3. Same as create request (through authorization)\n\n4. Watch Handler (pkg/endpoints/handlers/watch.go)\n\n   └─ Deserialize query parameters:\n      - resourceVersion: version to start watching from\n      - labelSelector, fieldSelector: filter objects\n      - timeoutSeconds: max watch duration\n\n   └─ Call storage.Watch(key, opts)\n      └─ Returns watch.Interface (stream of events)\n      └─ etcd connection establishes for this client\n      └─ Location: pkg/storage/etcd3/watcher.go\n\n   └─ HTTP Response Headers (200 OK)\n      └─ Content-Type: application/json\n      └─ Transfer-Encoding: chunked\n      └─ No Content-Length (streaming)\n\n   └─ Event Loop (runs until stream closed or timeout)\n      └─ For each event from watch.Interface:\n         ├─ Admission checks NOT applied to watch events\n         │  (admission already executed when object was created/modified)\n         ├─ Serialize event to ADDED/MODIFIED/DELETED JSON\n         ├─ Write event line to response stream\n         ├─ Flush to client\n         └─ Record event in audit if configured\n      └─ Blocks while waiting for next event\n      └─ Location: pkg/endpoints/handlers/watch.go:100-180\n\n   └─ Watch Termination Conditions:\n      - Client closes connection\n      - timeoutSeconds expires (default ~5-10 minutes)\n      - Watch event queue overflows (client too slow)\n      - Storage backend experiences error\n      - Server gracefully shutting down\n\n   └─ On Graceful Shutdown:\n      - New watches cannot start (429 or timeout)\n      - Existing watches drain in orderly fashion\n      - WithWatchTerminationDuringShutdown filter accelerates termination\n      - Location: pkg/server/filters/watch_termination.go\n\nTimeline:\n  T+0ms:     Watch request received\n  T+5ms:     Authentication/authorization completed\n  T+10ms:    Watch started, client receives 200 OK headers\n  T+10-300s: Events streamed to client as objects change\n  T+300s:    timeoutSeconds expires, connection closed\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 4.1 Failure Modes\n\n#### Graceful Degradation Under Failure\n\n| Failure Mode | Effect | Recovery |\n|---|---|---|\n| **Storage backend (etcd) down** | All write operations fail with 500 Internal Server Error; reads may work from cache | Automatic retry via client; server continues accepting requests |\n| **Admission webhook timeout** | Request times out (408 Request Timeout or context deadline); transaction fails | Webhook retried by admission chain; request fails; client can retry |\n| **Authentication service unavailable** | Requests using that authenticator fail (typically webhook-based) | Other authenticators may succeed (token, cert); token auth always available if configured |\n| **Authorization webhook unhealthy** | Requests queued/delayed pending webhook recovery; May eventually timeout | Server implements denial-of-service (DoS) protection via MaxInFlightLimit; requests rejected with 429 |\n| **Out of memory** | Server panics (caught by PanicRecovery filter); returns 500 error | Kubernetes restarts pod; requests in flight may be lost; persistent data safe in etcd |\n| **Goroutine leak in handler** | Memory grows; eventually OOM; affects responsiveness | Mitigated by request timeout enforcement; goroutines are backgrounded and will eventually be killed |\n| **Listener socket error** | HTTP server fails to bind port; StartFailed hook called; server cannot run | Must fix socket issue (port in use, permissions) and restart server |\n\n#### Request-Level Failures\n\n| Failure Type | Status Code | Effect |\n|---|---|---|\n| **Malformed URL** | 400 Bad Request | RequestInfo parsing fails; request rejected early (cannot route) |\n| **Unsupported API version** | 404 Not Found | Resource not registered; director finds no route |\n| **Authentication failed** | 401 Unauthorized | Authentication filter rejects; no user identity established |\n| **Authorization failed** | 403 Forbidden | Authorization filter rejects; user lacks permission |\n| **Admission rejected** | 400/422 Bad Request or Unprocessable Entity | Plugin policy violation; object fails validation/mutation |\n| **Optimistic concurrency conflict** | 409 Conflict | Update request includes stale resourceVersion; storage refuses write |\n| **Request timeout** | 408 Request Timeout | Handler did not complete before deadline; connection closed |\n| **Rate limit exceeded** | 429 Too Many Requests | PriorityAndFairness or MaxInFlightLimit rejected; retry-after header included |\n| **Object too large** | 413 Payload Too Large | Request body exceeds MaxRequestBodyBytes limit |\n| **Etcd write failure** | 500 Internal Server Error | Storage backend error; transaction failed; client should retry |\n\n### 4.2 Operational Limits\n\n#### Hard Limits (enforced by apiserver)\n\n| Limit | Default | Configurable | Implication |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **MaxRequestBodyBytes** | 3 MiB | Yes (Config.MaxRequestBodyBytes) | Requests larger than limit rejected with 413 |\n| **MinRequestTimeout** | 1 second | Yes | Clients cannot request shorter timeouts than this |\n| **RequestTimeout** | 60 seconds (default) | Yes | Long-running requests (watch) exempt; others cancelled |\n| **ShutdownTimeout** | Varies by impl. | Yes | Graceful shutdown aborted if exceeds timeout |\n| **MaxInFlightLimit** | 400 (or algorithm-based) | Yes via Config.MaxRequestsInFlightLimit | Excess requests queued or rejected with 429 |\n\n#### Soft Limits (policy-enforced)\n\n| Limit | Source | Effect | Tuning |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **List size** | Pagination (limit param) | Lists limited to batch size (default 100-1000 items) | Client must use continue token for large result sets |\n| **Watch event frequency** | Storage backend | Watch events may be batched; coalesced | Watch queue size affects latency; overflow causes watch termination |\n| **Concurrent connections** | OS socket limit | Server limited by ulimit -n (typically 1024-65535) | Requires OS-level tuning; affects total concurrent watches/requests |\n| **Storage key depth** | etcd design | Key paths limited to ~1000 chars | Affects namespace/name/subresource combinations |\n| **Object size** | Storage backend | Individual objects should be <1MB (etcd limit) | Large objects (images embedded in configmap) problematic |\n\n### 4.3 Design Tradeoffs\n\n#### Fail-Closed Security\n\n**Tradeoff**: All authorization/admission errors reject requests (fail-closed). This prevents authorization bypass but may cause false negatives.\n\n**Rationale**: Kubernetes prioritizes security over availability. Ambiguous authorization decisions must reject requests. This prevents privilege escalation.\n\n**Implication**: Misconfigured admission/authz policies can cause service outages. Requires careful policy development and testing.\n\n**Code location**: `pkg/admission/chain.go:70` - returns error immediately on first handler error.\n\n#### Request Filtering Order\n\n**Tradeoff**: Authentication happens before authorization. This means unauthenticated requests are rejected before authorization is checked.\n\n**Rationale**: Cannot make authorization decision without knowing who is requesting. Unauthenticated requests are always unauthorized anyway.\n\n**Implication**: Some authorization failures are masked by earlier auth failures. Cannot distinguish \"unauthorized\" from \"not authenticated\" without examining logs.\n\n#### Admission Plugins are Synchronous\n\n**Tradeoff**: Admission plugins execute synchronously in the request path. This means slow plugins delay all requests.\n\n**Rationale**: Admission must provide timely feedback to clients. Asynchronous admission would complicate retry logic.\n\n**Implication**: Slow admission webhooks impact API server latency for all users. Requires webhook timeout tuning and performance monitoring.\n\n#### Object Versioning is Implicit (Resource Version)\n\n**Tradeoff**: Objects track versions internally (resourceVersion field). Clients must manage versions for optimistic concurrency.\n\n**Rationale**: Implicit versioning simplifies API; clients see versions in responses. Explicit version objects would require separate APIs.\n\n**Implication**: Clients that ignore versions may cause lost updates. Requires client-side discipline and retry logic.\n\n#### Single Authorization Chain (Union)\n\n**Tradeoff**: Multiple authorizers are combined in a union (any \"Allow\" grants access; explicit \"Deny\" prevents access).\n\n**Rationale**: Allows composing multiple auth mechanisms (RBAC + ABAC + webhook). Flexible for varied deployment environments.\n\n**Implication**: Auth bugs in one component may leak access from another. Requires careful understanding of combined policies.\n\n#### Graceful Shutdown is Soft-Limited\n\n**Tradeoff**: Graceful shutdown waits for in-flight requests with timeout. Requests exceeding timeout are forcibly terminated.\n\n**Rationale**: Prevents indefinite hangs during shutdown. Balances politeness with responsiveness.\n\n**Implication**: Long-running requests may be killed during shutdown. Requires clients to handle connection drops and implement retry logic.\n\n#### Watch Streams Use HTTP Chunked Transfer Encoding\n\n**Tradeoff**: Watches use standard HTTP chunks instead of WebSockets or gRPC.\n\n**Rationale**: HTTP compatibility; works through most firewalls/proxies. Simpler protocol.\n\n**Implication**: Watch streams vulnerable to connection timeouts. Load balancers may terminate idle connections. Requires periodic keep-alive events.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 5.1 Extension Points for Consumers\n\n#### A. Custom Admission Plugins\n\n**Location**: `pkg/admission/interfaces.go`\n\n**How to extend:**\n```go\n// Implement admission.Interface\ntype MyPlugin struct {}\n\nfunc (p *MyPlugin) Handles(operation admission.Operation) bool {\n    return operation == admission.Create\n}\n\nfunc (p *MyPlugin) Admit(ctx, attributes admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces) error {\n    // Mutate object or reject request\n    return nil\n}\n\nfunc (p *MyPlugin) Validate(ctx, attributes admission.Attributes, o admission.ObjectInterfaces) error {\n    // Validate object without mutation\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n**Registration**: Add to admission chain during server config setup.\n\n**Risks**:\n- Plugin errors cause all requests to fail (fail-closed)\n- Slow plugins block all write operations\n- Plugins with bugs may corrupt data or cause privilege escalation\n- Plugins cannot distinguish between different API versions\n\n#### B. Custom Authentication Strategies\n\n**Location**: `pkg/authentication/authenticator/interfaces.go`\n\n**How to extend:**\n```go\n// Implement Token or Request authenticator\ntype MyAuthenticator struct {}\n\nfunc (a *MyAuthenticator) AuthenticateToken(ctx, token string) (*auth.Response, bool, error) {\n    // Parse token and return user.Info\n    return &auth.Response{User: userInfo}, true, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Registration**: Built into authenticator factory during config completion.\n\n**Risks**:\n- Auth bugs allow privilege escalation\n- Slow authenticators block all requests\n- Must handle secrets securely (never log tokens)\n\n#### C. Custom Authorization Strategies\n\n**Location**: `pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go`\n\n**How to extend:**\n```go\ntype MyAuthorizer struct {}\n\nfunc (a *MyAuthorizer) Authorize(ctx context.Context, attrs authorizer.Attributes) (authorizer.Decision, string, error) {\n    // Return Allow, Deny, or NoOpinion\n    return authorizer.DecisionAllow, \"allowed\", nil\n}\n```\n\n**Registration**: Combined in union authorizer during config completion.\n\n**Risks**:\n- Authorization bugs allow privilege escalation\n- NoOpinion decisions require fallback to other authorizers (may be unexpected)\n\n#### D. Custom Storage Backend\n\n**Location**: `pkg/storage/interfaces.go` and `pkg/registry/rest/rest.go`\n\n**How to extend:**\n```go\ntype MyStorage struct {}\n\n// Implement storage.Interface methods:\n// - Get, List, Create, Update, Delete, Watch\n// - Versioner interface for resource versioning\n\nfunc (s *MyStorage) Get(ctx, key string, opts storage.GetOptions) (runtime.Object, error) {\n    // Retrieve object from custom backend\n    return obj, nil\n}\n\nfunc (s *MyStorage) Create(ctx, key string, obj runtime.Object, ...) error {\n    // Write object to custom backend\n    return nil\n}\n```\n\n**Registration**: Provided via APIGroupInfo.VersionedResourcesStorageMap during InstallAPIGroups.\n\n**Risks**:\n- Storage bugs cause data loss or corruption\n- Slow storage blocks all requests\n- Watch implementation must be correct (difficult)\n- Consistency model affects application correctness\n\n#### E. Custom Handler Chain Builder\n\n**Location**: `pkg/server/config.go` (BuildHandlerChainFunc field)\n\n**How to extend:**\n```go\nconfig.BuildHandlerChainFunc = func(apiHandler http.Handler, c *Config) http.Handler {\n    // Add custom middleware\n    return myCustomMiddleware(apiHandler)\n}\n```\n\n**Integration**: Custom builder can wrap or replace DefaultBuildHandlerChain.\n\n**Risks**:\n- Incorrect filter order breaks authentication/authorization\n- Custom middleware may bypass security filters\n- Bugs in custom middleware affect all requests\n\n#### F. Health Check Plugins\n\n**Location**: `pkg/server/healthz/healthz.go`\n\n**How to extend:**\n```go\ntype MyHealthCheck struct {}\n\nfunc (h *MyHealthCheck) Check(req *http.Request) error {\n    // Check component health\n    return nil // healthy, or error if unhealthy\n}\n\n// Register\nconfig.HealthzChecks = append(config.HealthzChecks,\n    &server.HealthzChecks{\"mycheck\", MyHealthCheck{}})\n```\n\n**Integration**: Runs on /healthz, /livez, /readyz endpoints.\n\n**Risks**: Health check is synchronous; slow checks slow down monitoring.\n\n#### G. Lifecycle Hooks\n\n**Location**: `pkg/server/hooks.go`\n\n**PostStartHook**:\n```go\nserver.AddPostStartHook(\"my-hook\", func(context.Context) error {\n    // Runs after listener is ready, before serving requests\n    // Use for controller startup, cache initialization\n    return nil\n})\n```\n\n**PreShutdownHook**:\n```go\nserver.AddPreShutdownHook(\"my-hook\", func() error {\n    // Runs before graceful shutdown begins\n    // Use for cleanup, draining work\n    return nil\n})\n```\n\n**Risks**:\n- PostStartHook blocks server startup; must complete quickly\n- PreShutdownHook blocks shutdown; must complete before timeout\n\n### 5.2 Customization Hooks (for kube-apiserver)\n\nThe main kube-apiserver provides additional customization points on top of apiserver library:\n\n#### Install Custom Resources (`cmd/kube-apiserver/app/server.go`)\n\n**Location**: Main apiserver calls InstallAPIGroups for each group.\n\n**Customization**: Can register custom APIGroupInfo with custom storage.\n\n#### Custom Filters\n\n**Location**: kube-apiserver may wrap handler chain with additional filters.\n\n**Example**: Adding tracing filters, metrics, audit backends.\n\n#### Delegation Target\n\n**Location**: GenericAPIServer can delegate to another server (for aggregation).\n\n**Customization**: Can implement custom DelegationTarget for routing to extension servers.\n\n### 5.3 Risks and Security Considerations\n\n| Extension Point | Risk Level | Consideration |\n|---|---|---|\n| **Admission plugins** | **HIGH** | Plugins must handle all object types they claim to handle; bugs cause all writes to fail |\n| **Authentication strategies** | **CRITICAL** | Auth bugs allow privilege escalation; must protect secrets; never log authentication material |\n| **Authorization strategies** | **CRITICAL** | Auth bugs allow privilege escalation; NoOpinion decisions must be intentional |\n| **Storage backend** | **CRITICAL** | Data loss if storage is unreliable; watch implementation is complex; concurrency control critical |\n| **Handler chain builder** | **HIGH** | Can accidentally remove security filters; incorrect order breaks auth/authz |\n| **Health checks** | **LOW** | Slow health checks affect monitoring; unlikely to cause security issues |\n| **Lifecycle hooks** | **MEDIUM** | Blocking hooks delay startup/shutdown; hooks can access server state (be careful with concurrent access) |\n\n---\n\n## 6. Operational Implications and Considerations\n\n### 6.1 Performance Characteristics\n\n#### Request Latency Path\n\nTypical request latency breakdown (milliseconds):\n\n```\nDeserialization:         1-2 ms (JSON parsing)\nRequestInfo parsing:     0.5-1 ms (URL parsing, validation)\nAuthentication:          1-5 ms (token validation or cert verification)\nAuthorization:           1-5 ms (RBAC policy evaluation)\nAdmission (mutating):    2-20 ms (may call webhooks; network dependent)\nAdmission (validating):  2-20 ms (may call webhooks; network dependent)\nStorage write:           5-50 ms (etcd round-trip; network latency dominates)\nSerialization:           1-2 ms (JSON encoding)\n─────────────────────────────────\nTotal (typical):         15-150 ms\nTotal (webhook-heavy):   50-200+ ms\n```\n\n**Optimization opportunities:**\n- Admission webhook performance critical; slow webhooks delay all write operations\n- Storage backend latency dominates; etcd network latency matters\n- Authorization via webhook is expensive; RBAC is faster\n- Parallel authorization not implemented; sequential chain\n\n#### Throughput Limits\n\nPractical limits depend on:\n\n1. **Storage backend capacity**: etcd handles ~1000 writes/sec per server\n2. **MaxInFlightLimit**: Default limits concurrent requests (400-1000 typical)\n3. **Network bandwidth**: Response serialization must fit in available bandwidth\n4. **CPU cores**: Authentication/authorization is CPU-bound; scales with cores\n5. **Memory**: Object cache grows with dataset size; garbage collection pauses impact latency\n\n**Scaling strategies:**\n- Add more API server instances behind load balancer\n- Increase MaxInFlightLimit based on available resources\n- Optimize admission webhooks (cache results where possible)\n- Use RBAC instead of webhook authorization\n- Shard resources across multiple etcd clusters\n\n#### Watch Stream Characteristics\n\n- **Memory per watch**: ~1-10 MB per active watch (depends on queue size)\n- **Latency**: 10-100ms typical for event delivery (depends on event frequency)\n- **Throughput**: Thousands of concurrent watches per server (limited by memory)\n- **Reliability**: Watch streams must handle connection interruptions (no keepalive guarantee)\n\n### 6.2 Reliability and Availability\n\n#### High Availability Deployment\n\n```\n┌─────────────────┐\n│   Load Balancer │\n└────────┬────────┘\n         │\n    ┌────┴─────┬──────────┐\n    │           │          │\n┌───▼──┐    ┌──▼───┐   ┌──▼───┐\n│ API  │    │ API  │   │ API  │\n│ Srv1 │    │ Srv2 │   │ Srv3 │\n└───┬──┘    └──┬───┘   └──┬───┘\n    │          │          │\n    └──────┬───┴──────┬───┘\n           │          │\n        ┌──▼──────┬──▼──┐\n        │         │     │\n      ┌─▼──┐  ┌──▼─┐  ┌▼──┐\n      │etcd│  │etcd│  │etcd│\n      │ 1  │  │ 2  │  │ 3  │\n      └────┘  └────┘  └────┘\n```\n\n**Benefits**:\n- Single server failure doesn't affect availability\n- Load balancer distributes requests\n- etcd cluster provides data redundancy\n\n**Considerations**:\n- Load balancer must support long-lived watch connections (sticky sessions not needed; HTTP works)\n- Watch clients should handle reconnection and resume from resourceVersion\n- Cascading failures possible if load balancer flaps (all requests go to single server)\n\n#### Graceful Shutdown Sequence\n\nEnsuring minimal request loss during updates:\n\n```\n1. Signal shutdown (SIGTERM)\n   └─ ShutdownInitiated flag set\n   └─ Stop accepting config changes\n\n2. AfterShutdownDelayDuration (default 12 seconds)\n   └─ Time for load balancer to remove server from rotation\n   └─ New requests still accepted; routed to other servers\n\n3. NotAcceptingNewRequest threshold\n   └─ New requests rejected (429 Too Many Requests or connection timeout)\n   └─ In-flight requests allowed to complete\n\n4. InFlightRequestsDrained\n   └─ Wait for all non-watch requests to complete\n   └─ Timeout: ShutdownTimeout (default 30 seconds)\n   └─ If timeout exceeded, kill remaining requests\n\n5. HTTPServerStoppedListening\n   └─ HTTP listener closed\n   └─ No new TCP connections accepted\n\n6. AuditBackendShutdown\n   └─ Audit logs flushed to storage\n   └─ Audit backend closed\n```\n\n**Recommendation**: Set AfterShutdownDelayDuration to match load balancer drain time (typically 10-30 seconds).\n\n### 6.3 Security Hardening\n\n#### Authentication and Authorization\n\n**Recommendations**:\n- Enable multiple authentication methods (tokens, certs) for defense-in-depth\n- Use webhook authorization to enforce custom policies\n- Regularly audit authorization decisions (enable audit logging with high verbosity)\n- Implement rate limiting to prevent brute-force attacks\n- Rotate token signing keys and certificates regularly\n\n**Implementation**:\n- Webhook authenticators should use mTLS (client certificate verification)\n- Authorization webhooks should timeout quickly (~1 second) to prevent DoS\n- Cache authorization decisions where possible (reduces webhook latency)\n\n#### Admission Control\n\n**Recommendations**:\n- Enable Pod Security Policy (deprecated; use Pod Security Standards in 1.25+)\n- Enable Resource Quota for namespace isolation\n- Enable Network Policy admission\n- Validate webhook signatures (if using mutating/validating webhooks)\n\n**Implementation**:\n- Webhook admission should be on separate server with restricted access\n- Webhooks should use mTLS for authentication\n- Webhooks should fail-closed on timeout (reject requests)\n\n#### Audit Logging\n\n**Recommendations**:\n- Enable audit logging with RequestResponse level (logs request/response bodies)\n- Log to separate audit server (prevents log loss on API server failure)\n- Implement log retention and archival policies\n- Monitor audit logs for suspicious patterns\n\n**Implementation**:\n```\nAuditBackend configurations:\n- Log sink: local file, webhook, dynamic\n- Event levels: None, Metadata, RequestResponse\n- Sampling: Optional rate limiting to reduce log volume\n```\n\n#### Network Security\n\n**Recommendations**:\n- Enable HTTPS (TLS) for all communication\n- Use strong cipher suites (TLS 1.2+ with TLS_ECDHE_RSA_WITH_AES_128_GCM_SHA256 or better)\n- Implement network policies to restrict access to API server\n- Use API server authentication for kubelet requests (not recommended without client cert verification)\n\n### 6.4 Monitoring and Observability\n\n#### Key Metrics to Monitor\n\n| Metric | Source | Meaning | Alert Threshold |\n|---|---|---|---|\n| **apiserver_request_total** | Prometheus | Total requests by verb/resource/code | N/A (informational) |\n| **apiserver_request_duration_seconds** | Prometheus | Request latency (p50, p99) | p99 > 1s (investigate) |\n| **apiserver_dropped_requests_total** | Prometheus | Requests rejected by priority/fairness | > 0 (indicates overload) |\n| **apiserver_admission_webhook_rejection_count** | Prometheus | Admission webhooks rejecting requests | > threshold (policy too strict) |\n| **apiserver_authorization_decision_total** | Prometheus | Authorization decisions (allow/deny) | Deny spike (investigate) |\n| **apiserver_client_certificate_expiration_seconds** | Prometheus | Time until client certs expire | < 30 days (renew certs) |\n| **apiserver_webhook_latency** | Custom metrics | Webhook response time | > 100ms (slow webhooks) |\n| **etcd_request_duration_seconds** | Prometheus | etcd backend latency | > 100ms (investigate etcd) |\n| **process_resident_memory_bytes** | Prometheus | Memory usage | > 2GB typical (leak if grows unbounded) |\n| **scheduler_binding_duration_seconds** | Related | Time to bind pod (affected by apiserver latency) | > 1s (slow apiserver) |\n\n#### Health Checks\n\n```\nGET /healthz        → Simple liveness check (HTTP 200)\nGET /readyz         → Readiness check (includes all checks)\nGET /livez          → Liveness check (more detailed than /healthz)\nGET /livez?verbose  → Verbose liveness output (which checks passed/failed)\n```\n\n**Readiness probe typically includes**:\n- Storage backend connectivity\n- Admission webhook reachability\n- Authorization system availability\n\n**Liveness probe typically includes**:\n- HTTP server responding\n- No goroutine leaks\n- No panic hangs\n\n#### Logs to Monitor\n\n**Error-level logs**:\n- \"Authorization failed\" - Someone trying to access resources they shouldn't\n- \"Admission webhook timed out\" - Webhook is slow or unavailable\n- \"etcd connection error\" - Storage backend issues\n- \"context deadline exceeded\" - Requests timing out\n\n**Warning-level logs**:\n- \"Request took longer than X seconds\" - Performance degradation\n- \"Audit backend dropped events\" - Audit logging cannot keep up\n\n---\n\n## 7. Concise Map of Important Files and Directories\n\n### Core Server Files\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/server/genericapiserver.go` | Main GenericAPIServer struct (108-304 lines); lifecycle methods |\n| `pkg/server/config.go` | Config struct and builder (NewConfig, Complete, New methods) |\n| `pkg/server/handler.go` | APIServerHandler and routing logic (Director pattern) |\n| `pkg/server/hooks.go` | PostStartHook and PreShutdownHook infrastructure |\n| `pkg/server/secure_serving.go` | TLS/HTTPS listener setup |\n\n### Request Handling and Filters\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/server/filters/` | Server-level filters (panic, timeout, CORS, goaway, HTTP/2) |\n| `pkg/endpoints/filters/` | API-level filters (auth, authz, audit, request info) |\n| `pkg/server/mux/pathrecorder.go` | HTTP path multiplexing (non-REST routes) |\n\n### REST Handlers\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/endpoints/installer.go` | APIInstaller; registers REST endpoints for resources |\n| `pkg/endpoints/groupversion.go` | APIGroupVersion; manages a specific API group/version |\n| `pkg/endpoints/handlers/` | Individual handlers (create, get, list, patch, update, delete, watch) |\n\n### Admission Control\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/admission/interfaces.go` | Core admission interfaces (Interface, Attributes, ObjectInterfaces) |\n| `pkg/admission/chain.go` | ChainAdmissionHandler; executes plugins in order |\n| `pkg/admission/configuration/` | Dynamic webhook configuration management |\n\n### Authentication and Authorization\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/authentication/authenticator/interfaces.go` | Core authentication interfaces (Token, Request, Response) |\n| `pkg/authentication/request/` | Request-based authenticators (cert, basic, bearertoken) |\n| `pkg/authentication/authenticatorfactory/` | Factory for creating authenticators |\n| `pkg/authorization/authorizer/interfaces.go` | Core authorization interfaces (Authorizer, Attributes, Decision) |\n| `pkg/authorization/union/` | Union of multiple authorizers |\n\n### Storage and Registry\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/storage/interfaces.go` | Storage interfaces (Interface, Versioner, Lister, Getter, Watcher, etc.) |\n| `pkg/storage/etcd3/` | etcd3 backend implementation |\n| `pkg/storage/cacher/` | Caching layer above storage backends |\n| `pkg/registry/rest/rest.go` | REST storage interfaces and base types |\n\n### Utilities\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/server/routes/` | Route handlers (profiling, metrics, version, index) |\n| `pkg/server/healthz/` | Health check infrastructure |\n| `pkg/server/statusz/` | Status endpoint implementation |\n| `pkg/endpoints/discovery/` | API discovery and resource listing |\n| `pkg/util/` | Utility functions (requestinfo resolver, filters, etc.) |\n| `pkg/audit/` | Audit event logging |\n\n### Configuration and Options\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `pkg/server/options/` | Configuration options (admission, auth, authz, audit, etcd, etc.) |\n\n### Plugin System\n\n| Path | Purpose |\n|---|---|\n| `plugin/` | Plugin registration infrastructure |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Request Tracing Example: API Server Processing a Create Request\n\nTo solidify understanding, here's a concrete tracing of a single Create request through the entire system:\n\n### Request: Create a ConfigMap\n\n```bash\ncurl -X POST https://api.example.com/api/v1/namespaces/default/configmaps \\\n  -H \"Authorization: Bearer token123\" \\\n  -H \"Content-Type: application/json\" \\\n  -d '{\n    \"apiVersion\": \"v1\",\n    \"kind\": \"ConfigMap\",\n    \"metadata\": {\"name\": \"my-config\"},\n    \"data\": {\"key\": \"value\"}\n  }'\n```\n\n### Processing Trace\n\n1. **TCP Connection**: Client connects to API server listener (port 443)\n\n2. **TLS Handshake**: Client and server negotiate TLS session\n\n3. **HTTP Request Parse**: `net/http` parses request headers and body\n\n4. **Handler Invocation**: `APIServerHandler.ServeHTTP()` called (handler.go:187)\n\n5. **Filter Chain Execution** (config.go:1015-1097):\n   - **PanicRecovery**: Wraps handler with recover()\n   - **AuditInit**: Creates audit.Event, stores in ctx\n   - **MuxComplete**: Waits for routes (already complete)\n   - **RequestTimestamp**: ctx += RequestReceivedTimestamp\n   - **RequestInfo** (filters/request_info.go):\n     - Parses \"/api/v1/namespaces/default/configmaps\"\n     - Extracts: resource=\"configmaps\", verb=\"create\", namespace=\"default\"\n     - Validates path format\n   - **HTTPLogging**: Logs \"POST /api/v1/... user=system:serviceaccount:default:deployer\"\n   - **CORS**: Adds Access-Control-Allow headers (if origin matches)\n   - **TimeoutForNonLongRunning** (filters/timeout.go):\n     - Verb=\"create\" is not long-running\n     - Sets deadline = now + 60s (minRequestTimeout)\n     - Creates context with timeout\n   - **Deadline** (filters/request_deadline.go):\n     - Checks for \"timeout=Xs\" query param (not present)\n     - Continues with previous deadline\n   - **Authentication** (endpoints/filters/authentication.go):\n     - Finds Bearer token in Authorization header\n     - Token authenticator validates token (calls auth service)\n     - Returns user.Info: {Name: \"system:deployer\", UID: \"...\", Groups: [...]}\n     - Stores user in ctx\n   - **Impersonation** (endpoints/filters/impersonation/):\n     - No Impersonate-User header; user remains \"system:deployer\"\n   - **Audit** (endpoints/filters/audit.go - stage 1):\n     - Populates audit.Event fields: user, verb, resource, namespace\n     - Stores in ctx for later completion\n   - **PriorityAndFairness** (filters/priority_and_fairness.go or max_in_flight.go):\n     - Checks flow control (not queue; allows)\n     - Increments in-flight counter\n     - Defers decrement after request complete\n   - **Authorization** (endpoints/filters/authorization.go):\n     - Creates Attributes: {verb: \"create\", resource: \"configmaps\", namespace: \"default\", user: ...}\n     - Calls Authorizer.Authorize()\n     - RBAC checks: \"system:deployer\" has \"create configmaps\" permission in default namespace\n     - Decision: Allow\n   - **Next filter in chain** (continues to REST handler)\n\n6. **Director Routing** (handler.go:121-150):\n   - Path \"/api/v1/namespaces/default/configmaps\" matches REST pattern\n   - Routes to `GoRestfulContainer` (go-restful WebService)\n\n7. **REST Handler Invocation** (handlers/create.go):\n   - HTTP method=POST, path matches create action\n   - Routes to CreateResource handler\n\n8. **Request Deserialization** (handlers/create.go:58-120):\n   - Reads request body\n   - Determines content-type: application/json\n   - Uses configured serializer (runtime.NegotiatedSerializer)\n   - Unmarshals JSON → ConfigMap object\n   - Sets APIVersion=\"v1\", Kind=\"ConfigMap\"\n   - Validates required fields present\n\n9. **Admission - Mutating Phase** (handlers/create.go:125-140):\n   - Creates Attributes: {verb: \"create\", resource: \"configmaps\", namespace: \"default\", user: ...}\n   - Calls `admissionControl.Admit(attributes, objectInterfaces)`\n   - Each admission plugin runs:\n     - DefaultNamespace: (no-op for ConfigMap)\n     - ResourceDefaults: (no-op for ConfigMap)\n     - PodSecurityPolicy: (not applicable; not a Pod)\n     - Webhook plugins: CustomAdmissionWebhook runs\n       - POST to webhook URL with ConfigMap object\n       - Webhook reviews object and returns patch\n       - Patch applied to ConfigMap object\n   - Any plugin error returns 400; request aborted\n\n10. **Admission - Validating Phase** (handlers/create.go:140-160):\n    - Calls `admissionControl.Validate(attributes, objectInterfaces)`\n    - Each validating plugin runs:\n      - ObjectFieldSelector: (no-op)\n      - ResourceQuota: Checks namespace quota for configmaps\n        - Quota allows 100 configmaps; 50 already exist\n        - Decision: Allow\n      - Webhook plugins: CustomValidatingWebhook runs\n        - POST to webhook URL with ConfigMap object\n        - Webhook validates object (checks data is valid YAML, etc.)\n        - Returns allow decision\n    - Any plugin error returns 422 Unprocessable Entity; request aborted\n\n11. **Storage Write** (handlers/create.go:165-180):\n    - Calls `storage.Create(ctx, key, obj, out, ttl)`\n    - Key = \"/configmaps/default/my-config\"\n    - etcd backend receives write request:\n      - Establishes connection to etcd\n      - Sends PUT request with object data\n      - etcd writes object and increments revision (resource version)\n      - Returns success with revision number\n    - Storage layer sets obj.metadata.resourceVersion = revision\n    - Stores object reference in `out` parameter\n\n12. **Audit - Response Phase** (endpoints/filters/audit.go - stage 2):\n    - Enriches audit.Event with response fields:\n      - Status: 201 Created\n      - Response object: ConfigMap (if configured to log)\n    - Submits event to audit backend\n    - Backend may log to file, webhook, or discard (depends on policy)\n\n13. **HTTP Response** (handlers/create.go:180-200):\n    - Status: 201 Created\n    - Headers:\n      - Content-Type: application/json; charset=utf-8\n      - Location: /api/v1/namespaces/default/configmaps/my-config\n    - Body: Full ConfigMap object (JSON serialized)\n      ```json\n      {\n        \"apiVersion\": \"v1\",\n        \"kind\": \"ConfigMap\",\n        \"metadata\": {\n          \"name\": \"my-config\",\n          \"namespace\": \"default\",\n          \"uid\": \"12345678-...\",\n          \"resourceVersion\": \"98765432\",\n          \"creationTimestamp\": \"2024-03-01T10:30:00Z\"\n        },\n        \"data\": {\"key\": \"value\"}\n      }\n      ```\n\n14. **Response Sent**: HTTP stream sends response to client\n\n15. **Cleanup**:\n    - In-flight request counter decremented\n    - Request removed from wait group\n    - Request processing complete\n\n### Timeline Summary\n\n- T+0ms: Request received at listener\n- T+1ms: RequestInfo extracted; verb/resource determined\n- T+2ms: Authentication completed; user identified\n- T+3ms: Authorization completed; permission verified\n- T+5ms: Admission plugins executed; object potentially mutated\n- T+8ms: etcd write issued (network latency begins)\n- T+50ms: etcd response received; resource version assigned\n- T+52ms: Response serialized and sent\n- T+55ms: Client receives 201 Created with ConfigMap object\n- T+60ms: Request completely cleaned up; removed from wait group\n\n**Total latency: ~55-60ms (dominated by etcd network roundtrip)**\n\n---\n\n## Conclusion\n\nThe Kubernetes apiserver library provides a sophisticated, composable framework for building Kubernetes-compatible API servers. Its layered architecture cleanly separates concerns (routing, auth, admission, storage) while maintaining flexibility for customization. Understanding the request-path flow, extension points, and operational characteristics is essential for effectively deploying, tuning, and extending the system.\n\nThe fail-closed security design, explicit admission phases, and graceful lifecycle management prioritize correctness and availability. Operational success requires careful attention to admission webhook performance, storage backend health, and graceful shutdown configuration.\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

I've created a comprehensive architecture and extension guide for the Kubernetes apiserver library. The document is saved at `/workspace/documentation.md`.\n\n## Summary of Contents\n\nThe documentation covers:\n\n### 1. **Subsystem Scope** (§1)\n- Purpose: Generic framework for Kubernetes-compatible API servers\n- Boundaries: Internal components vs. external consumer responsibilities\n- Dependencies: Upstream (apimachinery, kube-openapi) and downstream (kube-aggregator, extension servers)\n\n### 2. **Key Components** (§2)\n- **GenericAPIServer**: Central orchestrator with state and lifecycle methods\n- **Handler Chain**: Ordered middleware stack (25 filters) from panic recovery through authorization\n- **Admission Control**: Two-phase (mutating/validating) plugin chain with fail-closed semantics\n- **Authentication/Authorization**: Pluggable strategies with
